Being vegan is always a personal choice but I'm slowly learning about the different environmental impact from the vegan alternatives. There always seems to be a lot of confusion as sometimes the vegan options are not more environmentally friendly. (for example if the meat substitute cannot be produced in your country due to the climate, emissions from transport and shipping can be huge just to get it to you, let alone the impacts from actually producing it - so actually there would be less emissions if you bought locally sourced meat) (and also for 100ml of almond milk it takes 1 litre of water to produce enough almonds) I feel like there is a lot of confusion on both sides of the argument though.  It's all very interesting though. I'm studying an animal science degree at university and its got a lot of content on nutrition, livestock production and global food security and its interesting to see what's going on in the food production world. apparently some places are looking into feeding cows on seaweed to reduce their methane emissions and feeding pigs on insects to help give them better protein content also meaning more grain goes to human food rather than pig food.  From what I've learnt, people can be vegan for whatever reasons (animal welfare, personal preference, health issues) but when it come to doing it for the environment, its a really murky subjects because you can't just look at the emissions and impact of production from the meat industry, you have to look at the emissions and impact of production for the alternatives you are choosing  Don't have a go at me, I'm just telling you what we are being taught by professors and lectures who's whole career is studying this stuff and then teaching it to us

Just on the vegan topic: Colleen is absolutely right and it was well said. I am vegan and have been for a couple of years now. When I first transitioned it was really tricky  weening myself off certain meals I was used to. I think one of the most important things about changing diets drastically is taking it in increments, for lack of a better term never go "cold turkey". You can do yourself serious damage that way without even realising it. I highly recommend just doing your research, see a dietitian to adequately plan your meals so as to be sure you are getting enough nutrition and be patient. Being vegan is not the cure to anything and definitely doesn't work for everyone and that's totally fine. Any bit of effort to just be more ethical is a great thing. At the end of the day your health and wellbeing should come first.  That's my two cents

Since the beginning of 2019, members of the National Assembly of France have introduced 29 bills pertaining to the French Bioethics Law, which is revised every seven years. These bills have asked the government to establish a department to register human organ transplants, tracking the sources of organs from foreign countries, and enacting more dissuading punishment to curb organ trafficking.  More and more evidence found in recent years has identified China as the major source of organ trafficking and removal of organs from people without consent.  Falun Gong practitioners in Paris staged a rally on the plaza outside the National Assembly on October 1, asking Assembly members to support a new law to stop the forced organ harvesting crimes in China. Falun Gong practitioners are the largest group of prisoners of conscience targeted for forced organ harvesting by the Chinese Communist regime.     Falun Gong practitioners demonstrated the exercises and held a rally outside of the National Assembly of France.  Several members of the Assembly have introduced bills to amend the organ donation protocols of the current Bioethics Law, aiming to stop organ trafficking, and to uphold basic ethics and morality.  France is the first country in Europe to propose that a government entity must register and maintain records concerning organ transplants that were performed in foreign countries. If the law passes, it will make France the leader in a multi-country collaboration to administer organ transplantation.  Other proposals include setting up a blacklist to target organ traffickers, and more severe punishments to prosecute individuals benefiting from organ trafficking. Since September 24, the 29 proposed bills were discussed and voted on in the Assembly.  HervÃ© Saulignac, Assembly member representing the Department of ArdÃ¨che, stated that it is very important to inform the French people about what is happening in China.  â€œI mean,â€ he said, â€œthere are organs taken without the consent of the person. I've been vegan for 3.5 years at this point and have watched your channel for even longer. I think it would be great for you to go vegan, but it took me about 4 months to fully transition, and took another year or two to fully get acclimated. For anyone who wants to try, go slow, start with small things, and don't try to be perfect. The truest definition of veganism is in the pursuit of eliminating harm towards animals and the planet as much as possible in your life. Also, I'd recommend cutting cheese out of your diet, then giving yourself like 4-6 months to get acclimated to not craving cheese (due to the Casein in cheese), then trying a couple of different vegan cheeses. There are some great ones out there, and they're only getting better!

I was vegan for a while and I was definitely the super annoying, very strict vegan and then I started having some health issues and it was very important that i had food that would help sustain my body. i realized that being considerate to veganism while also understanding that im living i a non-vegan world is important and that even eating vegan for even just a few days out of each week can still make a huge impact over time!
I'm a vegetarian and it took me a really long time to cut out meat from my diet. I first became a pescetarian because I don't like the taste of pork, chicken, and turkey. I then eventually cut out seafood. Next, I stopped eating eggs. The easiest part for me was switching to oat milk and vegan butter because I can't taste a difference from cows milk. I still eat cheese and sometimes I'll eat prepared foods that contain regular milk and butter on occasion. It was hard at times and everybody reacts differently to changes in a food diet. I'm the kind of vegetarian who will inform people by giving them resources if they want it. I don't force anybody. I just do me and you can do whatever you want and we'll see what happens.

Bravo to making our own choices and to each their own when it comes to how they want to eat in life. Scientifically-speaking though, without pasture-raised animals and their manures as well as wild animals dying naturally, we wouldn't have enough nutrients in the soil to support the amount of farmed crops that we would need to sustain our food needs should everyone become vegan. Most plants farmed for human consumption are heavy feeders and rely on living soil microbes to process nutrients that plants can use to grow.  Also, humans need B-12 and lots of fats to support their "big brains" (thank you evolution!) and B-12 comes naturally from meat, eggs and dairy sources only. Thus, it's important to supplement with B-12 if you eat a vegan diet. Just my $0.02.

Just a reminder that becoming vegan might be the best choice for you or for your family, but it might not be the best or safest choice for others. People with certain disabilities or chronic illnesses often have a list of foods that they consider "safe" foods and sometimes those foods aren't vegan. These safe foods are things that those people know won't cause their disabilities/illnesses to go into a panic mode (basically causing their body to become sick or cause an allergic reaction which could put them in the hospital - no one wants to go there during a global pandemic if they don't have to). I don't want this to sound mean but I feel like THIS specific part of the debate isn't thought about or talked about enough.
